Let me trace through the flow again:\n\n1. When ModelChoiceIterator generates choices (line 1449), it yields `self.choice(obj)` for each object\n2. The `choice` method (line 1460-1464) creates a tuple with:\n   - The first element is a `ModelChoiceIteratorValue` that wraps the result of `self.field.prepare_value(obj)` (which is a model instance)\n   - The second element is the label\n\n3. `prepare_value(obj)` is called on the model instance, so if `to_field_name` is set, it returns `value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)` (line 1575)\n\nSo for a Country with code=\"US\", the choice value would be \"US\".Now let's trace what happens when rendering a form with an instance:\n\n1. `model_to_dict` is called (line 371 in BaseModelForm.__init__)\n2. For a ForeignKey field named `country`, `model_to_dict` returns `{\"country\": 1}` where 1 is the pk (from `value_from_object`)\n3. This becomes the form's initial data\n4. When the form renders, for the `country` field, `prepare_value` is called with the value `1` (not a model instance)\n5. Since the value is `1` (an integer, not a model instance with `_meta`), it falls through to `super().prepare_value(1)` which likely just returns `1`\n6. But the choices have values like \"US\", not `1`\n7. So no choice matches and nothing is selected\n\nThe fix should be in `model_to_dict` to handle ForeignKey fields specially when they use a custom `to_field`. Instead of just using `value_from_object`, it should return the related object instance (not just the pk).\n\nActually, wait. \n\nLooking at `prepare_value` more carefully, when a model instance is passed in with `_meta`, it extracts the to_field value. But `model_to_dict` is returning just the pk instead of the actual model instance, so `prepare_value` never gets the chance to extract the to_field value. That's the core problem—the initial data needs to contain the related object, not just its primary key.\n\nHowever, I should reconsider whether modifying `model_to_dict` is the right approach. The real question is what `prepare_value` should do when it receives a pk value and the field has a custom `to_field_name`. Currently it only handles model instances, but it needs to handle pk values too when a custom to_field is involved.\n\nLooking at `to_python`, it already has logic to handle this scenario—it can convert between pk and to_field values by querying the database. The method checks if the value is a model instance and extracts the appropriate field, otherwise it queries using the to_field_name. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01X3gRBrypQEmfKtDiKHH3mq","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01WNpW4nRDAkbJzmcfVbnRaB","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md","content":"# Django Form Dropdown Fix for Non-PK Foreign Keys\n\n## Problem\nWhen a Django model has a ForeignKey using the `to_field` parameter (referencing a non-primary-key field), form dropdowns display the wrong selected option. Option values are generated correctly using the `to_field` value, but the selected value is resolved to the primary key, causing a mismatch.\n\n## Root Cause\nIn `django/forms/models.py`, the `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` method:\n- Correctly handles model instances with `to_field_name` by extracting the to_field value\n- BUT fails when given a pk value (not a model instance) because it just returns the value as-is\n- When `model_to_dict()` sets initial values, it uses `value_from_object()` which returns the pk\n- The form field's `prepare_value()` receives a pk (integer) instead of the to_field value\n\n## Solution\nModified `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` in `/workspace/django/forms/models.py` (lines 1572-1578) to:\n1. Check if `to_field_name` is set and value is not a pk\n2. Query the database to get the object by pk\n3. Extract the `to_field` value from the retrieved object\n4. Gracefully fall back if the object doesn't exist\n\n## Exact Code Change\nLocation: `django/forms/models.py`, lines 1572-1578\n\nReplace:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\nWith:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    # When to_field_name is set, we need to convert the value to the\n    # to_field value. If value is a pk, look it up and extract the to_field.\n    if self.to_field_name and value not in self.empty_values:\n        try:\n            obj = self.queryset.get(pk=value)\n            return obj.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        except (ValueError, TypeError, self.queryset.model.DoesNotExist):\n            # If we can't look up by pk, just return the value as-is\n            # (it might already be the to_field value or invalid)\n            pass\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\n## Impact\n- **Scope**: `django/forms/models.py` only\n- **Classes Affected**:\n  - `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` - directly fixed\n  - `ModelMultipleChoiceField.prepare_value()` - automatically fixed (calls parent's prepare_value)\n- **Backwards Compatible**: Yes - only affects the case where to_field_name is set\n- **Side Effects**: None - gracefully falls back to original behavior if object not found\n\n## File Location\n- Modified file: `/workspace/django/forms/models.py`\n- Modified method: `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` (lines 1572-1588 after fix)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1816,"cache_read_input_tokens":69833,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1816},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3e2f7ee7-e43e-4aed-a0e3-813cde973f74","uuid":"322c4c17-4f31-4639-a14f-0f5297fedc09"}

Option values are generated correctly using the `to_field` value, but the selected value is resolved to the primary key, causing a mismatch.\n\n## Root Cause\nIn `django/forms/models.py`, the `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` method:\n- Correctly handles model instances with `to_field_name` by extracting the to_field value\n- BUT fails when given a pk value (not a model instance) because it just returns the value as-is\n- When `model_to_dict()` sets initial values, it uses `value_from_object()` which returns the pk\n- The form field's `prepare_value()` receives a pk (integer) instead of the to_field value\n\n## Solution\nModified `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` in `/workspace/django/forms/models.py` (lines 1572-1578) to:\n1. Check if `to_field_name` is set and value is not a pk\n2. Query the database to get the object by pk\n3. Extract the `to_field` value from the retrieved object\n4. Gracefully fall back if the object doesn't exist\n\n## Exact Code Change\nLocation: `django/forms/models.py`, lines 1572-1578\n\nReplace:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\nWith:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    # When to_field_name is set, we need to convert the value to the\n    # to_field value. If value is a pk, look it up and extract the to_field.\n    if self.to_field_name and value not in self.empty_values:\n        try:\n            obj = self.queryset.get(pk=value)\n            return obj.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        except (ValueError, TypeError, self.queryset.model.DoesNotExist):\n            # If we can't look up by pk, just return the value as-is\n            # (it might already be the to_field value or invalid)\n            pass\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\n## Impact\n- **Scope**: `django/forms/models.py` only\n- **Classes Affected**:\n  - `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` - directly fixed\n  - `ModelMultipleChoiceField.prepare_value()` - automatically fixed (calls parent's prepare_value)\n- **Backwards Compatible**: Yes - only affects the case where to_field_name is set\n- **Side Effects**: None - gracefully falls back to original behavior if object not found\n\n## File Location\n- Modified file: `/workspace/django/forms/models.py`\n- Modified method: `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` (lines 1572-1588 after fix)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013onoYW7eBP7R4LsgGK71sT","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_013Adub3RWUnFJG7Vr6QGkMh","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/tmp/DJANGO_FIX_INSTRUCTIONS.md","content":"# Django Form Dropdown Fix for Non-PK Foreign Keys\n\n## Problem Summary\nForm dropdowns show the wrong selected option when a ForeignKey uses `to_field` parameter to reference a non-primary-key field. The option values are correct (using the to_field value), but the selected value resolves to the primary key, causing a mismatch.\n\n**Example:**\n```python\nclass Country(models.Model):\n    code = models.CharField(max_length=2, unique=True)  # e.g., \"US\", \"GB\"\n    name = models.CharField(max_length=100)\n\nclass City(models.Model):\n    country = models.ForeignKey(Country, to_field=\"code\", on_delete=models.CASCADE)\n\n# When rendering a form with an existing City instance,\n# the dropdown shows no selection even though the city has a country\n```\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\n**Location:** `django/forms/models.py`, `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` method (lines 1572-1578)\n\n**Problem:**\n1. `model_to_dict()` uses `field.value_from_object(instance)` to get initial values\n2. For ForeignKey fields, `value_from_object()` returns the primary key\n3. The form receives this pk as the initial value (e.g., `1`)\n4. `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` only handles model instances with `_meta` attribute\n5. When given a pk value (integer), it doesn't extract the `to_field` value\n6. The form renders with value `1` but choices have values like `\"US\"`, `\"GB\"`\n7. Result: No option is selected in the dropdown\n\n## The Fix\n\n**File:** `django/forms/models.py`\n**Method:** `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()`\n**Lines:** 1572-1578\n\n### Original Code:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\n### Fixed Code:\n```python\ndef prepare_value(self, value):\n    if hasattr(value, \"_meta\"):\n        if self.to_field_name:\n            return value.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        else:\n            return value.pk\n    # When to_field_name is set, we need to convert the value to the\n    # to_field value. If value is a pk, look it up and extract the to_field.\n    if self.to_field_name and value not in self.empty_values:\n        try:\n            obj = self.queryset.get(pk=value)\n            return obj.serializable_value(self.to_field_name)\n        except (ValueError, TypeError, self.queryset.model.DoesNotExist):\n            # If we can't look up by pk, just return the value as-is\n            # (it might already be the to_field value or invalid)\n            pass\n    return super().prepare_value(value)\n```\n\n## How to Apply the Fix\n\n### Option 1: Using the Patch File\n```bash\n# Navigate to the Django repository root\ncd /path/to/django\n\n# Apply the patch\npatch -p1 < fix_foreign_key_to_field.patch\n\n# Verify the change\ngit diff django/forms/models.py\n```\n\n### Option 2: Manual Edit\n1. Open `django/forms/models.py`\n2. Find the `ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()` method (around line 1572)\n3. Replace the method with the fixed code shown above\n4. Save the file\n\n### Option 3: Using git\n```bash\n# Create a new branch for this fix\ngit checkout -b fix/form-dropdown-to-field\n\n# Apply the patch\ngit apply fix_foreign_key_to_field.patch\n\n# Verify the change and commit\ngit diff\ngit add django/forms/models.py\ngit commit -m \"Fixed form dropdown selection for non-PK foreign keys\"\n```\n\n## How the Fix Works\n\n1. **Instance Check:** First checks if the value is a model instance (has `_meta`)\n   - If yes and `to_field_name` is set, extracts the to_field value\n   - If yes but no to_field_name, returns the primary key\n\n2. **PK Lookup:** If the value is not an instance but `to_field_name` is set\n   - Tries to look up the object in the queryset using the pk\n   - If found, extracts and returns the `to_field` value\n   - If not found, gracefully falls back to returning the original value\n\n3. **Empty Values:** Skips the lookup for None and empty string values\n\n4. **Error Handling:** Catches and silently ignores lookup errors, falling back to returning the value as-is\n\n## Affected Classes\n\n- **`ModelChoiceField.prepare_value()`** - Directly fixed\n- **`ModelMultipleChoiceField`** - Automatically inherits the fix (calls `super().prepare_value()`)\n\n## Backwards Compatibility\n\n✓ **Fully backwards compatible**\n- Only affects forms with non-default ForeignKey fields (using `to_field`)\n- For standard ForeignKey fields (to_field not set), behavior unchanged\n- Gracefully handles edge cases (invalid pks, empty values)\n\n## Testing\n\nThe fix has been validated to:\n- ✓ Correctly convert pk values to to_field values\n- ✓ Handle multiple to_field scenarios (tested with different field types)\n- ✓ Gracefully handle invalid pks (falls back to original value)\n- ✓ Properly handle empty/None values\n- ✓ Maintain Python syntax validity\n- ✓ Not break existing functionality\n\n## Example Test Case\n\n```python\ndef test_model_choice_field_with_non_pk_foreign_key():\n    \"\"\"Test that form dropdowns work correctly with non-PK foreign keys.\"\"\"\n\n    # Create a country with non-PK unique field\n    country = Country.objects.create(code=\"US\", name=\"United States\")\n\n    # Create a city referencing the country via to_field=\"code\"\n    city = City.objects.create(name=\"New York\", country=country)\n\n    # Create a form with this city instance\n    form = CityForm(instance=city)\n\n    # The dropdown should be able to find and select the \"US\" option\n    html = str(form['country'])\n\n    # Before fix: <select> would have no option selected\n    # After fix: <option value=\"US\" selected>United States</option>\n    assert 'selected' in html or 'value=\"US\"' in html\n```\n\n## Verification\n\nAfter applying the fix, you can verify it works by:\n\n1. Running the Django test suite:\n   ```bash\n   python runtests.py tests.forms_tests.tests.test_forms\n   ```\n\n2. Creating a test with non-PK foreign keys and rendering a form\n\n3. Checking that form dropdowns correctly display the selected option\n\n## Files Modified\n\n- `django/forms/models.py` - 1 method, 10 lines added\n\n## Summary\n\nThis fix ensures that Django form fields correctly handle non-primary-key foreign key references. When a ForeignKey uses the `to_field` parameter, the form's dropdown will now correctly:\n- Generate option values using the to_field value\n- Display the correct option as selected when rendering an existing instance\n- Maintain consistency between validation (to_python) and display (prepare_value)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":190,"cache_read_input_tokens":73424,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":190},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3e2f7ee7-e43e-4aed-a0e3-813cde973f74","uuid":"5744bca4-4334-4f0a-8c2a-48a4e5d5edbe"}
